## Copilot
To ensure that the text formatting remains the same as in the template, you need to handle the text replacement more carefully. The `python-docx` module allows you to manipulate runs within a paragraph to preserve formatting.

Here's an updated version of your functions to preserve formatting:

### Updated Functions

```python
from docx import Document

# Define a function to replace text in a run, preserving formatting
def replace_text_in_run(run, old_text, new_text):
    if old_text in run.text:
        run.text = run.text.replace(old_text, new_text)

# Define a function to replace text in the document while preserving formatting
def replace_text(doc, old_text, new_text):
    for paragraph in doc.paragraphs:
        for run in paragraph.runs:
            replace_text_in_run(run, old_text, new_text)
    for table in doc.tables:
        for row in table.rows:
            for cell in row.cells:
                for paragraph in cell.paragraphs:
                    for run in paragraph.runs:
                        replace_text_in_run(run, old_text, new_text)

# Define a function to create new forms with different information
def create_form(template_path, output_path, replacement_dict):
    # Load the template document
    doc = Document(template_path)
    
    # Replace the text in the document while preserving formatting
    for old_text, new_text in replacement_dict.items():
        replace_text(doc, old_text, new_text)
    
    # Save the new document
    doc.save(output_path)

# Example usage
template_path = "template.docx"
output_path = "output.docx"
replacement_dict = {
    "NAME_PLACEHOLDER": "Alice Johnson",
    "DOB_PLACEHOLDER": "01 January 2000",
    "GENDER_PLACEHOLDER": "Female",
    "ADDRESS_PLACEHOLDER": "123 Elm Street",
    "POSTCODE_PLACEHOLDER": "AB1 2CD",
    "PHONE_PLACEHOLDER": "1234567890"
}
create_form(template_path, output_path, replacement_dict)
```

### Explanation:

1. **Preserve Formatting in Runs**:
   - The `replace_text_in_run` function handles text replacement within a `run` while preserving formatting.
   - The `run.text.replace(old_text, new_text)` method replaces the text within the run.

2. **Replace Text in Paragraphs and Tables**:
   - The `replace_text` function iterates through paragraphs and tables, accessing each run within paragraphs to replace the text.

3. **Create Form with Preserved Formatting**:
   - The `create_form` function loads the template document, replaces text while preserving formatting, and saves the new document.

Using these updated functions, the text formatting in your documents will remain consistent with the template, even after replacements. This should give you well-formatted forms with the updated information.

## Copilot
It seems that some replacements are not being made, possibly due to text runs being split or the text being formatted in a way that isn't captured by the current replacement logic. Let's make sure we're handling these cases properly by iterating over each run within paragraphs and cells more carefully.

Here's an updated version of the functions that should address this issue:

### Updated Functions

```python
from docx import Document

# Define a function to replace text in a run, preserving formatting
def replace_text_in_run(run, old_text, new_text):
    if old_text in run.text:
        run.text = run.text.replace(old_text, new_text)

# Define a function to replace text in the document while preserving formatting
def replace_text(doc, old_text, new_text):
    for paragraph in doc.paragraphs:
        for run in paragraph.runs:
            replace_text_in_run(run, old_text, new_text)
    for table in doc.tables:
        for row in table.rows:
            for cell in row.cells:
                for paragraph in cell.paragraphs:
                    for run in paragraph.runs:
                        replace_text_in_run(run, old_text, new_text)

# Define a function to create new forms with different information
def create_form(template_path, output_path, replacement_dict):
    # Load the template document
    doc = Document(template_path)
    
    # Replace the text in the document while preserving formatting
    for old_text, new_text in replacement_dict.items():
        # First, replace text using existing method
        replace_text(doc, old_text, new_text)
        
        # Additional check to ensure all instances are replaced
        for paragraph in doc.paragraphs:
            if old_text in paragraph.text:
                inline = paragraph.runs
                for i in range(len(inline)):
                    if old_text in inline[i].text:
                        text = inline[i].text.replace(old_text, new_text)
                        inline[i].text = text
                        
        for table in doc.tables:
            for row in table.rows:
                for cell in row.cells:
                    for paragraph in cell.paragraphs:
                        if old_text in paragraph.text:
                            inline = paragraph.runs
                            for i in range(len(inline)):
                                if old_text in inline[i].text:
                                    text = inline[i].text.replace(old_text, new_text)
                                    inline[i].text = text

    # Save the new document
    doc.save(output_path)

# Example usage
template_path = "template.docx"
output_path = "output.docx"
replacement_dict = {
    "Adele Gibson": "Calista Gardner",
    "Female": "Binary",
    "24.09.06": "25.09.06",
    "72 Cranberry Road BD33 6TY": "45-49 The Headrow LS97 1QE",
    "01274566666": "07106298342",
    "Sheila Haddock": "Abigail Collingwood",
    "Brainstree Street SM4 7YM": "422 Bradford Rd LS46 9FQ",
    "09999966668": "07359903420",
    "BPwell Academy": "Blue Sky International"
}
create_form(template_path, output_path, replacement_dict)
```

### Explanation:

1. **Replace Text in Runs**:
   - The `replace_text_in_run` function replaces text within a run while preserving formatting.

2. **Iterate Through Paragraphs and Tables**:
   - The `replace_text` function iterates through all paragraphs and tables, replacing text within runs.

3. **Additional Check for All Instances**:
   - Within the `create_form` function, an additional check ensures all instances of the text are replaced within paragraphs and table cells. This step ensures that any split runs are also handled properly.

4. **Updated Example Usage**:
   - An example usage demonstrates how to use the updated functions with your replacement dictionary.

This should help ensure that all instances of the specified text are replaced correctly while preserving the formatting. If you encounter any further issues, feel free to let me know!

## Me
Brief summary of the business problem (reason) for undertaking this project and the benefits of the outcomes to the stakeholders.  

## Copilot
The AI Document Extraction Program is being undertaken to address the inefficiencies and inaccuracies in manually processing and extracting information from various document types. In many organizations, valuable time and resources are spent on manually sifting through documents to identify and extract key data points, which can lead to human errors, delays, and increased operational costs.

### Business Problem
Manually processing large volumes of documents is time-consuming and prone to errors. This not only affects productivity but also leads to inconsistencies in data extraction, which can impact decision-making processes. The reliance on manual labor for document handling can result in high operational costs and limited scalability.

### Benefits to Stakeholders
1. **Increased Efficiency**: Automating the document extraction process will significantly reduce the time and effort required to process documents, leading to faster turnaround times and improved productivity.
2. **Enhanced Accuracy**: AI-powered extraction ensures a higher level of accuracy and consistency in data extraction, minimizing the risk of human errors and improving data quality.
3. **Cost Savings**: By reducing the need for manual labor, organizations can lower operational costs and allocate resources more effectively.
4. **Scalability**: The AI Document Extraction Program enables organizations to scale their operations efficiently, handling larger volumes of documents without a proportional increase in workload.
5. **Better Decision-Making**: Access to accurate and timely data empowers stakeholders to make informed decisions, driving better business outcomes and strategic planning.

Overall, this project aims to streamline document processing, enhance data accuracy, and provide significant cost savings, ultimately leading to improved operational efficiency and stakeholder satisfaction.

## Me
Next question: How will the Financial Benefits be measured?  

## Copilot
The financial benefits of the AI Document Extraction Program will be measured using a combination of quantitative and qualitative metrics. Here’s how:

### 1. Cost Savings:
- **Labor Cost Reduction**:
  - Measure the reduction in hours spent on manual data entry and document processing before and after implementation.
  - Calculate the cost savings by multiplying the reduction in hours by the average hourly wage of employees previously performing these tasks.
  
- **Error Correction Cost Savings**:
  - Track the number of errors and associated costs (e.g., rework, compliance issues) before and after the program is implemented.
  - Measure the reduction in error-related costs over time.

### 2. Productivity Gains:
- **Processing Time**:
  - Measure the average time taken to process a document before and after the AI solution is implemented.
  - Calculate the increase in processing capacity and estimate the productivity gains in terms of the number of additional documents processed per unit of time.
  
- **Turnaround Time**:
  - Track the time from document submission to completion before and after implementation.
  - Measure the reduction in turnaround time and its impact on overall operational efficiency.

### 3. Improved Decision-Making:
- **Data Availability**:
  - Measure the time taken to make critical data available for decision-making processes before and after the program is implemented.
  - Evaluate the impact of timely data availability on decision-making quality and speed.
  
- **Data Accuracy**:
  - Conduct periodic audits to assess the accuracy of data extracted by the AI solution compared to manual extraction.
  - Measure the reduction in discrepancies and their impact on decision-making.

### 4. Compliance and Risk Management:
- **Regulatory Compliance**:
  - Track the number of compliance-related issues and associated costs before and after implementation.
  - Measure the reduction in fines, penalties, and other compliance-related costs.
  
- **Security Incidents**:
  - Monitor the frequency and impact of data breaches or unauthorized access incidents before and after implementation.
  - Calculate the reduction in costs associated with security incidents.

### 5. Strategic Resource Allocation:
- **Resource Reallocation**:
  - Track the reallocation of resources from manual data entry to more strategic tasks and measure the financial impact.
  - Evaluate the increase in revenue or cost savings resulting from resource reallocation to higher-value activities.

### Summary:
By systematically tracking these metrics, the organization can quantify the financial benefits of the AI Document Extraction Program and demonstrate its positive impact on cost savings, productivity gains, improved decision-making, compliance, and strategic resource allocation. These measurements will provide valuable insights into the program’s effectiveness and support continuous improvement efforts.

### Service Benefits

The AI Document Extraction Programme brings several service benefits that enhance operational efficiency, service quality, and stakeholder satisfaction:

- **Resource Optimization:** By reducing the time spent on manual data entry and document processing, staff can focus on higher-value tasks such as case analysis, client interaction, and strategic planning.

**2. Improved Data Quality:**
- **Consistency and Accuracy:** AI ensures that data extracted from documents is consistent and accurate, reducing errors and discrepancies. This leads to more reliable data for decision-making and reporting.
- **Real-time Updates:** Automated extraction provides real-time updates to databases and records, ensuring that information is always current and reflective of the latest inputs.

**3. Better Decision-Making:**
- **Timely Access to Information:** Accurate and promptly extracted data enables stakeholders to make informed decisions quickly. This is particularly critical in child social care, where timely interventions can significantly impact outcomes.
- **Comprehensive Data Insights:** AI can analyze patterns and trends across large volumes of data, offering valuable insights that can inform policy decisions and improve service delivery strategies.

**4. Enhanced Compliance:**
- **Regulatory Adherence:** Automated document processing ensures that all required information is accurately captured and reported, maintaining compliance with regulatory standards. This reduces the risk of fines and legal issues.
- **Audit Readiness:** Consistent and accurate data management facilitates easier and more efficient audits, providing confidence to regulatory bodies and stakeholders.

**5. Increased Stakeholder Satisfaction:**
- **Client Experience:** Faster and more accurate document processing improves the overall experience for clients, who receive timely and reliable service. This enhances trust and satisfaction among service users.
- **Staff Morale:** By alleviating the burden of repetitive manual tasks, the programme improves job satisfaction and morale among staff, leading to a more motivated and productive workforce.

**6. Scalability and Flexibility:**
- **Adaptable Solutions:** The AI solution can easily scale to handle increasing volumes of documents, making it adaptable to growing service demands. This ensures that the service can continue to operate efficiently even as workloads increase.
- **Customizable Workflows:** The programme can be tailored to fit specific service needs and workflows, providing flexibility to address unique requirements and challenges.

Overall, the AI Document Extraction Programme enhances service efficiency, improves data quality, supports better decision-making, ensures compliance, increases stakeholder satisfaction, and offers scalability and flexibility. ## Me
Is there a legislative reason for this IT Requirements Document?  

## Copilot
There may indeed be legislative reasons for creating an IT Requirements Document, especially for projects involving sensitive data, such as child social care forms. Here are a few potential legislative reasons:

1. **Data Protection Laws**: Compliance with data protection laws such as the General Data Protection Regulation (GDPR) ensures that personal data is processed lawfully, fairly, and transparently. The IT Requirements Document helps outline the measures taken to protect sensitive information.

2. **Regulatory Compliance**: Adhering to regulations specific to social care and safeguarding children, such as the Children Act 1989 and 2004 in the UK, ensures that the technology used meets the required standards and supports the welfare of children.

3. **Audit and Accountability**: Creating a detailed IT Requirements Document provides a clear record of the system's specifications and compliance measures, which can be essential during audits or inspections by regulatory bodies.

4. **Security Standards**: Ensuring that the IT system complies with established security standards, such as ISO/IEC 27001, helps protect against data breaches and unauthorized access, which is crucial for maintaining trust and integrity.

By addressing these legislative reasons in the IT Requirements Document, the project ensures compliance with relevant laws and regulations, supporting the safe and effective use of technology in processing sensitive information.  

## Me
Have any initial Risks been identified?  

## Copilot
Yes, several initial risks have been identified for the AI Document Extraction Program. These include:

### 1. Data Privacy and Security:
- **Risk**: Unauthorized access or data breaches involving sensitive information.
- **Mitigation**: Implement robust encryption, access controls, and regular security audits to protect data.

### 2. Compliance Issues:
- **Risk**: Failure to comply with data protection regulations (e.g., GDPR).
- **Mitigation**: Ensure compliance with all relevant regulations through regular reviews and updates to policies and procedures.

### 3. System Reliability:
- **Risk**: System downtime or failures impacting document processing.
- **Mitigation**: Develop a robust infrastructure with redundancy and failover mechanisms, and perform regular maintenance.

### 4. Accuracy of Data Extraction:
- **Risk**: AI model inaccuracies leading to incorrect data extraction.
- **Mitigation**: Continuously train and validate the AI model with diverse datasets to improve accuracy and reliability.

### 5. Resistance to Change:
- **Risk**: Stakeholder resistance to adopting new technology.
- **Mitigation**: Provide comprehensive training, support, and communication to ensure smooth adoption and user buy-in.

### 6. Integration Challenges:
- **Risk**: Difficulties integrating the AI system with existing systems.
- **Mitigation**: Conduct thorough testing and work closely with IT teams to ensure seamless integration.

### 7. Ethical Concerns:
- **Risk**: Ethical issues related to AI decision-making and data usage.
- **Mitigation**: Establish clear ethical guidelines and governance frameworks to address potential concerns.

These risks will be carefully monitored and managed throughout the project to ensure successful implementation and operation of the AI Document Extraction Program.

## Copilot
Sure, here’s how you can categorize the identified risks:

### Financial Risks:
- **Labor Cost Savings**: Potential underestimation of labor savings may not yield expected financial benefits.
- **Error Correction Savings**: Overestimation of error-related cost savings might not reflect actual financial gains.
- **Compliance Fines**: Unforeseen fines due to non-compliance can impact budget allocations.

### Operational Risks:
- **Data Privacy and Security**: Unauthorized access or data breaches could disrupt operations.
- **System Reliability**: Downtime or system failures affecting document processing capabilities.
- **Accuracy of Data Extraction**: Inaccurate AI model leading to incorrect data extraction and operational inefficiencies.
- **Integration Challenges**: Difficulties integrating the AI system with existing systems, potentially causing delays and disruptions.
- **Resistance to Change**: Stakeholder resistance to adopting new technology affecting smooth implementation.

### Reputational Risks:
- **Accuracy of Data Extraction**: Persistent inaccuracies may damage the organization’s reputation.
- **Compliance Issues**: Non-compliance with data protection regulations could harm the organization's public image.
- **Ethical Concerns**: Public perception of ethical issues related to AI decision-making may negatively impact the organization’s standing.

### Statutory Risks:
- **Data Privacy and Security**: Non-compliance with data protection laws like GDPR could result in legal consequences.
- **Compliance Issues**: Failure to adhere to regulations specific to social care and safeguarding children can result in statutory penalties.
- **Regulatory Compliance**: Ensuring adherence to all applicable regulations and standards to avoid legal and statutory repercussions.

By categorizing the risks this way, you can develop targeted mitigation strategies for each category, ensuring a comprehensive risk management approach for the AI Document Extraction Program.

## Me
EIA/DPIA assessments  

## Copilot
**EIA (Environmental Impact Assessment)** and **DPIA (Data Protection Impact Assessment)** are two distinct types of assessments used for different purposes:

### Environmental Impact Assessment (EIA)
An EIA evaluates the potential environmental effects of a proposed project or development before it is carried out. It aims to ensure that decision-makers consider environmental impacts when deciding whether to proceed with a project. Key components include:
- **Screening**: Determining whether a project requires an EIA.
- **Scoping**: Identifying which potential impacts are relevant to assess.
- **Impact Analysis**: Predicting the likely environmental effects.
- **Mitigation**: Proposing measures to reduce adverse impacts.
- **Reporting**: Documenting the findings in an Environmental Impact Statement (EIS).
- **Decision-making**: Using the EIS to inform the approval process.
- **Monitoring**: Ensuring that mitigation measures are implemented and effective.

### Data Protection Impact Assessment (DPIA)
A DPIA is a process to help identify and minimize the data protection risks of a project. It is mandatory under the GDPR for projects that are likely to result in a high risk to individuals' rights and freedoms. Key components include:
- **Description of Processing**: Detailing the nature, scope, context, and purposes of the processing.
- **Necessity and Proportionality**: Assessing whether the processing is necessary and proportionate.
- **Risk Assessment**: Identifying and evaluating risks to individuals' rights and freedoms.
- **Mitigation Measures**: Proposing measures to mitigate identified risks.
- **Consultation**: Consulting with data protection officers, stakeholders, and, where appropriate, individuals.
- **Documentation**: Keeping a record of the DPIA process and outcomes.

Both assessments are crucial for ensuring responsible and sustainable project planning, whether it's protecting the environment or safeguarding personal data. Do you have a specific project in mind that requires either of these assessments?

(Now Wednesday, Feb 19)  
End of questions for IT Requirements Document.  
How can I refactor this code, given that extracted_documents is now a 7x7 array where each sub-array is a certain form_type, previously it was just a 1D array with 7 items (one for each form_type):  

```Python
# Loop through each form type and extract features
for form_type, config in configurations.items():
    for doc_text in extracted_documents:
        features = extract_features(doc_text, config)
        combined_features = {f"{form_type}_{k}": v for k, v in features.items()}
        data.append(combined_features)
        labels.append(form_type)
```  

## Copilot
To refactor the code to handle a 7x7 array where each sub-array corresponds to a certain form type, you need to loop through each sub-array within `extracted_documents`. Here’s how you can do it:

```python
# Loop through each form type and extract features
for form_type, config in configurations.items():
    # Access the sub-array for the current form type
    for doc_text in extracted_documents[form_type]:
        features = extract_features(doc_text, config)
        combined_features = {f"{form_type}_{k}": v for k, v in features.items()}
        data.append(combined_features)
        labels.append(form_type)
```

### Explanation:

1. **Outer Loop**: Loop through each form type and its configuration using `for form_type, config in configurations.items():`.
2. **Inner Loop**: Instead of looping through `extracted_documents` directly, loop through `extracted_documents[form_type]` to access the sub-array corresponding to the current form type.
3. **Feature Extraction**: Extract features from each document text in the sub-array using `extract_features(doc_text, config)`.
4. **Combine Features**: Combine the extracted features with the form type prefix.
5. **Append to Data and Labels**: Append the combined features to `data` and the form type to `labels`.

This way, you ensure that each document within the sub-arrays is processed correctly, and the features are extracted and labeled accordingly.

## Copilot
A 404 error typically indicates that the server was unable to find the requested resource. Here are a few things to check and suggestions to potentially resolve the issue:

1. **Verify the File Path**: Ensure that the `DOWNLOADS_FOLDER` path in your app's configuration is correct and that the filename exists in that directory.

2. **Check File Path Construction**: Make sure the file path is being constructed correctly and that it points to the right location.

3. **Permissions**: Verify that the server has permission to read the file in the specified directory.

4. **Debug Logging**: Add debug logging to print the file path and verify it matches the expected location.

Here's an updated version of your code with additional debug logging:

```python
import os
from flask import flash, redirect, url_for, send_from_directory

def download_file(filename):
    try:
        # Ensure the file exists
        file_path = os.path.join(app.config['DOWNLOADS_FOLDER'], filename)
        print(f"Checking file path: {file_path}")  # Debug logging
        if not os.path.exists(file_path):
            flash('File not found')
            thisAutoLogger.addToLogs('File not found')
            return redirect(url_for('index'))
        
        # Send the file for download
        response = send_from_directory(app.config['DOWNLOADS_FOLDER'], filename, as_attachment=True)
        response.headers["Content-Disposition"] = f"attachment; filename={filename}"
        return response
    except Exception as e:
        flash('Error downloading file: {}'.format(str(e)))
        thisAutoLogger.addToErrorLogs('Error downloading file: {}'.format(str(e)))
        return redirect(url_for('index'))
```

### Explanation:
1. **Debug Logging**: Added a print statement to log the file path being checked. This helps verify that the path is correct.
2. **Permissions**: Make sure the server has read permissions for the files in the `DOWNLOADS_FOLDER`.

### Additional Tips:
- **Flask Configuration**: Ensure `app.config['DOWNLOADS_FOLDER']` is set correctly in your Flask application configuration.
- **Check Filename**: Confirm that the filename passed to `download_file()` matches the actual file name, including case sensitivity.
- **Flask Static Folder**: If the files are located in a static directory, consider using Flask's built-in support for serving static files.

By adding these checks and logging, you can better diagnose the issue and ensure that the correct file path is being used. If the problem persists, the debug logs should provide more insight into the cause of the 404 error.

### 1. Ensure URL Encoding:

### 2. Verify Flask Static Folder:
- Ensure that the file is in the correct directory and accessible. Flask by default serves static files from a folder named `static`. If you’re using a different folder, you need to specify the path correctly.

### 3. Check File Path and URL Consistency:
- Verify that the file path in the `send_from_directory` function matches the actual file location and the URL used for the download request.

Here’s an updated version of your code with URL encoding:

```python
import os
from flask import flash, redirect, url_for, send_from_directory, safe_join

def download_file(filename):
    try:
        # Ensure the file exists
        file_path = safe_join(app.config['DOWNLOADS_FOLDER'], filename)
        print(f"Checking file path: {file_path}")  # Debug logging
        if not os.path.exists(file_path):
            flash('File not found')
            thisAutoLogger.addToLogs('File not found')
            return redirect(url_for('index'))
        
        # Send the file for download
        response = send_from_directory(app.config['DOWNLOADS_FOLDER'], filename, as_attachment=True)
        response.headers["Content-Disposition"] = f"attachment; filename={filename}"
        return response
    except Exception as e:
        flash('Error downloading file: {}'.format(str(e)))
        thisAutoLogger.addToErrorLogs('Error downloading file: {}'.format(str(e)))
        return redirect(url_for('index'))

# Example usage
outFolder = 'Other AI Projects/AI Document Extraction/doc/testDocs'
app.config['DOWNLOADS_FOLDER'] = outFolder

# Debug print to confirm paths
print(f"DOWNLOADS_FOLDER: {app.config['DOWNLOADS_FOLDER']}")
```

By following these steps, you can ensure that the file path and URL are correctly handled, reducing the chances of encountering a 404 error. If the issue persists, please provide additional details or logs to help further diagnose the problem.

def download_file(filename):

## Me
Can I serve the file from the static folder and where this need to be relative to my project structure, my current output folder is 'Other AI Projects/AI Document Extraction/doc/testDocs'?  

## Copilot
Yes, you can serve the file from the static folder in Flask. The static folder should be located within your project structure and can be accessed directly via URL paths.

Here’s how you can set it up:

### 1. Move Files to the Static Folder
Move your output files to the static folder within your project directory. Create the static folder if it doesn't already exist. The structure would look like this:

```
your_project/
│
├── app.py (your Flask app)
├── static/
│   └── testDocs/
│       ├── New A & E Case 1.docx
│       ├── New A & E Case 2.docx
│       └── New A & E Case 3.docx
├── templates/
│   └── index.html
└── Other AI Projects/AI Document Extraction/doc/ (original output folder)
```

### 2. Update the File Path in Your Code
Modify your code to reference the files in the static folder:

```python
import os
from flask import Flask, send_from_directory, url_for, redirect, flash

app = Flask(__name__)

# Define the static folder
app.config['STATIC_FOLDER'] = os.path.join(app.root_path, 'static/testDocs')

@app.route('/download/<filename>')
def download_file(filename):
    try:
        # Ensure the file exists
        file_path = os.path.join(app.config['STATIC_FOLDER'], filename)
        print(f"Checking file path: {file_path}")  # Debug logging
        if not os.path.exists(file_path):
            flash('File not found')
            return redirect(url_for('index'))
        
        # Send the file for download
        return send_from_directory(app.config['STATIC_FOLDER'], filename, as_attachment=True)
    except Exception as e:
        flash(f'Error downloading file: {str(e)}')
        return redirect(url_for('index'))

# Run the app
if __name__ == '__main__':
    app.run(debug=True)
```

### 3. Accessing the Files via URL
Once the files are in the static folder and your Flask app is running, you can access and download the files via URLs like this:

```
http://127.0.0.1:5000/download/New%20A%20E%20Case%201.docx
```

### Summary
- Move your output files to the `static/testDocs` folder within your project.
- Update your Flask code to reference the new location of the files.
- Access the files via the appropriate URLs.

By following these steps, you can serve the files from the static folder and avoid the 404 errors. If you encounter any issues, feel free to let me know!  

## Me
How can I use this method in the html to download teh file?  
`href="{{ url_for('static', filename='styles.css') }}"`  
I already have this code that retrieves the file name:  
`const urlParams = new URLSearchParams(window.location.search);`  
`const filepath = urlParams.get('filepath');`  

## Copilot
To use the retrieved file name and create a download link in your HTML, you can modify the `href` attribute dynamically using JavaScript. Here’s an example of how to achieve this:

### HTML:
```html
<!DOCTYPE html>
<html lang="en">
<head>
    <meta charset="UTF-8">
    <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0">
    <title>Download File</title>
</head>
<body>
    <!-- This link will be updated dynamically -->
    <a id="download-link" href="#">Download File</a>

    <!-- Your existing script to retrieve the file path -->
    <script>
        const urlParams = new URLSearchParams(window.location.search);
        const filepath = urlParams.get('filepath');

        // Set the href attribute dynamically
        if (filepath) {
            const downloadLink = document.getElementById('download-link');
            downloadLink.href = `/static/testDocs/${filepath}`;
            downloadLink.innerText = `Download ${filepath}`;
        }
    </script>
</body>
</html>
```

### Explanation:
1. **HTML Structure**: You have an anchor tag `<a id="download-link">` that will be updated dynamically.
2. **JavaScript Code**: After retrieving the `filepath` parameter, you dynamically set the `href` attribute of the anchor tag.
    - **Construct the URL**: Assuming the files are in the `static/testDocs` folder, construct the URL accordingly.
    - **Update the Link**: Set the `href` attribute of the anchor tag to the constructed URL and update the link text.

This way, the download link will be dynamically updated based on the file path retrieved from the URL parameters. When the user clicks on the link, the browser will download the file from the specified path.  

## Me
No so I just want to use this but with the filepath parameter:  
`href="{{ url_for('static', filename='styles.css') }}"`  

## Copilot
You can use the `url_for` function in your HTML to create a dynamic download link using the `filepath` parameter. Here’s how you can do it:

### HTML:
```html
<!DOCTYPE html>
<html lang="en">
<head>
    <meta charset="UTF-8">
    <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0">
    <title>Download File</title>
</head>
<body>
    <!-- This link will be updated dynamically with the filepath parameter -->
    <a id="download-link" href="#">Download File</a>

    <!-- Your existing script to retrieve the file path -->
    <script>
        const urlParams = new URLSearchParams(window.location.search);
        const filepath = urlParams.get('filepath');

        // Set the href attribute dynamically using url_for format
        if (filepath) {
            const downloadLink = document.getElementById('download-link');
            downloadLink.href = `{{ url_for('static', filename='testDocs/') }}${filepath}`;
            downloadLink.innerText = `Download ${filepath}`;
        }
    </script>
</body>
</html>
```

### Explanation:
1. **HTML Structure**: You have an anchor tag `<a id="download-link">` that will be updated dynamically.
2. **JavaScript Code**: 
   - After retrieving the `filepath` parameter, the script dynamically sets the `href` attribute of the anchor tag.
   - The `url_for` function is used to generate the URL for the static folder, and the retrieved `filepath` parameter is appended to it.
   - This will create a valid URL to download the file from the static folder.

By following these steps, the `href` attribute of the download link will be dynamically updated to point to the correct file path based on the `filepath` parameter. When the user clicks on the link, the browser will download the file from the specified path.  

## Me
Is there a way to download it automatically after the link has been set and not include this link on the page?  

## Copilot
Yes, you can trigger the download automatically without displaying the link on the page. You can achieve this by creating a hidden link element and programmatically clicking it with JavaScript. Here's how you can do it:

### HTML:
```html
<!DOCTYPE html>
<html lang="en">
<head>
    <meta charset="UTF-8">
    <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0">
    <title>Download File</title>
</head>
<body>
    <!-- Hidden link element -->
    <a id="download-link" style="display: none;"></a>

    <!-- Your existing script to retrieve the file path -->
    <script>
        const urlParams = new URLSearchParams(window.location.search);
        const filepath = urlParams.get('filepath');

        // Set the href attribute dynamically and trigger download
        if (filepath) {
            const downloadLink = document.getElementById('download-link');
            downloadLink.href = `{{ url_for('static', filename='testDocs/') }}${filepath}`;
            downloadLink.download = filepath;

            // Programmatically click the link to trigger download
            downloadLink.click();
        }
    </script>
</body>
</html>
```

### Explanation:
1. **Hidden Link Element**: The anchor tag `<a id="download-link" style="display: none;"></a>` is hidden using the `display: none;` style.
2. **JavaScript Code**: 
   - After retrieving the `filepath` parameter, the script dynamically sets the `href` attribute of the hidden anchor tag.
   - The `download` attribute is set to ensure the file is downloaded with the correct name.
   - The script programmatically clicks the hidden link to trigger the download.

By using this approach, the download will be initiated automatically without displaying the link on the page.

How can I write javascript and a flask route for when teh user uploads a file (without pressing any other buttons) using the input with id 'file-upload'? The javascript should activate as soon as the file is uploaded, send to teh flask route the uploaded file. The flask route should then take this file, check if it's already been uploaded and if it has call the 'determineFormType' method with the name of this file as the only parameter of aforementioned method. It should finally return teh output of that method and redirect back to index. Upon receival of this 'predicted_form_type' variable, the javascript should set the value of teh select with id 'form-type' to this variable. If the file hasn't been uploaded, teh flask route should return None and the javascript should keep the select teh same.  

## Copilot
Here’s how you can achieve this with a combination of JavaScript and Flask:

### HTML with JavaScript:
Update your HTML to include JavaScript that listens for file upload and sends the file to the Flask route:

```html
<!DOCTYPE html>
<html lang="en">
<head>
    <meta charset="UTF-8">
    <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0">
    <title>Upload File</title>
</head>
<body>
    <form id="upload-form" action="/upload" method="post" enctype="multipart/form-data">
        <label for="file-upload">File Upload</label>
        <input type="file" id="file-upload" name="file" accept=".doc, .docx">

        <label for="convertToDocument">Document to Convert To</label>
        <input type="file" id="convertToDocument" name="convertToDocument" required>

        <label for="output-file-name">Output File Name</label>
        <input type="text" id="output-file-name" name="output-filename" placeholder="Enter output file name">
        
        <label for="form-type">Form Type (more info can be found <a href="https://bcft-ai.pythonprogrammertutorials.me/Other AI Projects/AI Document Extraction/markdown/formTypesExplanation">here)</a></label>
        <select id="form-type" name="form-type">
            <option value="Default">Default</option>
            <option value="Case 1">Case 1</option>
            <option value="Case 2">Case 2</option>
            <option value="Case 3">Case 3</option>
            <option value="A & E Case 1">A & E Case 1</option>
            <option value="A & E Case 2">A & E Case 2</option>
            <option value="A & E Case 3">A & E Case 3</option>
        </select>
        
        <div class="button-container">
            <button type="submit">Upload</button>
            <button type="button" onclick="submitProcessForm()">Extract Info</button>
        </div>
    </form>

    <script>
        document.getElementById('file-upload').addEventListener('change', function() {
            const formData = new FormData();
            formData.append('file', this.files[0]);

            fetch('/upload', {
                method: 'POST',
                body: formData
            })
            .then(response => response.json())
            .then(data => {
                if (data.predicted_form_type) {
                    document.getElementById('form-type').value = data.predicted_form_type;
                }
            })
            .catch(error => console.error('Error:', error));
        });
    </script>
</body>
</html>
```

### Flask Route:
Create a Flask route to handle the file upload, check if the file has been uploaded, call the `determineFormType` method, and return the result:

```python
from flask import Flask, request, jsonify, redirect, url_for
import os

app = Flask(__name__)
app.config['UPLOAD_FOLDER'] = 'Other AI Projects/AI Document Extraction/doc/testDocs'

def determineFormType(filename):
    # Dummy implementation, replace with actual logic
    return "Case 1" if "Case 1" in filename else "Default"

@app.route('/upload', methods=['POST'])
def upload_file():
    if 'file' not in request.files:
        return jsonify(None)

    file = request.files['file']
    filename = file.filename
    file_path = os.path.join(app.config['UPLOAD_FOLDER'], filename)

    if os.path.exists(file_path):
        predicted_form_type = determineFormType(filename)
        return jsonify({'predicted_form_type': predicted_form_type})

    return jsonify(None)

@app.route('/')
def index():
    return 'Index Page'

if __name__ == '__main__':
    app.run(debug=True)
```

### Explanation:
1. **HTML with JavaScript**:
   - Listens for changes on the file input with `id='file-upload'`.
   - Creates a `FormData` object and appends the selected file.
   - Sends the file to the `/upload` Flask route using the Fetch API.
   - Receives the `predicted_form_type` from the response and sets the value of the select input with `id='form-type'`.

2. **Flask Route**:
   - Handles the file upload in the `/upload` route.
   - Checks if the uploaded file exists in the specified directory.
   - If it exists, calls `determineFormType` to get the form type and returns it as JSON.
   - If not, returns `None`.

By using this approach, the file upload is handled automatically, and the form type is set based on the uploaded file without additional user input.  

## Me
There's an issue with my ML model, this is the code for it, however it always predicts 'A & E Case 3' except for when it's 'Case 3' it predicts 'Case 3' correctly, my training data uses 7 of each type of form, how can I fix this?  

```Python
import re
import pandas as pd
from sklearn.model_selection import train_test_split
from sklearn.impute import SimpleImputer
from sklearn.naive_bayes import MultinomialNB
from sklearn.metrics import accuracy_score, classification_report
import joblib

from documentExtraction import documentExtractor
from form_configurations import formConfigurationStorer as formCfS
from autoLogger import *

folderName = 'Other AI Projects/AI Document Extraction/src/localFiles'
thisAutoLogger = general_logger(f"{folderName}/run_logs.txt")

# Define form configurations
thisFormCfS = formCfS()
formTypes = [
    "Default",
    "Case 1",
    "Case 2",
    "Case 3",
    "A & E Case 1",
    "A & E Case 2",
    "A & E Case 3"
]
form_configs = thisFormCfS.get_all_configs()
configurations = dict(zip(formTypes, form_configs))

# Store text from all relevant extracted documents
docExt = documentExtractor()
extracted_documents = {}
for formType in formTypes:
    thisRow = []
    if formType == "Case 2":
        formName = formType.lower()
    elif formType == "Default":
        formName = "Example filled Breaking Cycles Referral Form"
    else:
        formName = formType
    text = docExt.extract_text_from_docx(f"{folderName}/{formName}.docx", form_type=formType)
    thisRow.append(text)
    for num in range(6):
        text = docExt.extract_text_from_docx(f"{folderName}/{formName} ({num+1}).docx", form_type=formType)
        thisRow.append(text)
    extracted_documents[formType] = thisRow

# Function to extract features based on patterns
def extract_features(text, config):
    features = {}
    for key, pattern in config['patterns'].items():
        match = re.search(pattern, text)
        features[key] = bool(match)
    return features

# Example dataset
data = []
labels = []

# Loop through each form type and extract features
for form_type, config in configurations.items():
    # Access the sub-array for the current form type
    for doc_text in extracted_documents[form_type]:
        features = extract_features(doc_text, config)
        combined_features = {f"{form_type}_{k}": v for k, v in features.items()}
        data.append(combined_features)
        labels.append(form_type)

# Convert to DataFrame
df = pd.DataFrame(data)
df['label'] = labels

# Encode labels
X = df.drop('label', axis=1)
y = df['label']

# Impute missing values with a placeholder (e.g., False)
imputer = SimpleImputer(strategy='constant', fill_value=False)
X_imputed = imputer.fit_transform(X)

# Split the data into training and testing sets
X_train, X_test, y_train, y_test = train_test_split(X_imputed, y, test_size=0.2, random_state=42)

# Train a Naive Bayes classifier
model = MultinomialNB()
model.fit(X_train, y_train)

# Save the model and configurations
joblib.dump(model, folderName+'/../form_type_model.joblib')
joblib.dump(configurations, folderName+'/../form_configurations.joblib')

# Predict on the test set
y_pred = model.predict(X_test)

# Evaluate the model
accuracy = accuracy_score(y_test, y_pred)
print(f"Accuracy: {accuracy}")
print(classification_report(y_test, y_pred))
```  

## Copilot
It seems like your model is overfitting to the 'A & E Case 3' class, and you might have an imbalance issue in your feature set or training data. Here are a few steps you can take to address this:

### 1. Check Feature Distribution
Ensure that the features are evenly distributed across different classes. If some classes have unique features, the model might be biased towards them.

### 2. Balance the Training Data
Even though you have 7 samples for each form type, it's essential to ensure that your features are representative and varied.

### 3. Use Feature Scaling
Scale your features to ensure that no feature dominates others.

### 4. Try Different Classifiers
Naive Bayes assumes independence between features, which might not be the case. Try using different classifiers like Random Forest or SVM.

### Example Code with Feature Scaling and Different Classifier:

```python
import re
import pandas as pd
from sklearn.model_selection import train_test_split
from sklearn.impute import SimpleImputer
from sklearn.preprocessing import StandardScaler
from sklearn.ensemble import RandomForestClassifier
from sklearn.metrics import accuracy_score, classification_report
import joblib

from documentExtraction import documentExtractor
from form_configurations import formConfigurationStorer as formCfS
from autoLogger import *

folderName = 'Other AI Projects/AI Document Extraction/src/localFiles'
thisAutoLogger = general_logger(f"{folderName}/run_logs.txt")

# Define form configurations
thisFormCfS = formCfS()
formTypes = [
    "Default",
    "Case 1",
    "Case 2",
    "Case 3",
    "A & E Case 1",
    "A & E Case 2",
    "A & E Case 3"
]
form_configs = thisFormCfS.get_all_configs()
configurations = dict(zip(formTypes, form_configs))

# Store text from all relevant extracted documents
docExt = documentExtractor()
extracted_documents = {}
for formType in formTypes:
    thisRow = []
    if formType == "Case 2":
        formName = formType.lower()
    elif formType == "Default":
        formName = "Example filled Breaking Cycles Referral Form"
    else:
        formName = formType
    text = docExt.extract_text_from_docx(f"{folderName}/{formName}.docx", form_type=formType)
    thisRow.append(text)
    for num in range(6):
        text = docExt.extract_text_from_docx(f"{folderName}/{formName} ({num+1}).docx", form_type=formType)
        thisRow.append(text)
    extracted_documents[formType] = thisRow

# Function to extract features based on patterns
def extract_features(text, config):
    features = {}
    for key, pattern in config['patterns'].items():
        match = re.search(pattern, text)
        features[key] = bool(match)
    return features

# Example dataset
data = []
labels = []

# Loop through each form type and extract features
for form_type, config in configurations.items():
    # Access the sub-array for the current form type
    for doc_text in extracted_documents[form_type]:
        features = extract_features(doc_text, config)
        combined_features = {f"{form_type}_{k}": v for k, v in features.items()}
        data.append(combined_features)
        labels.append(form_type)

# Convert to DataFrame
df = pd.DataFrame(data)
df['label'] = labels

# Encode labels
X = df.drop('label', axis=1)
y = df['label']

# Impute missing values with a placeholder (e.g., False)
imputer = SimpleImputer(strategy='constant', fill_value=False)
X_imputed = imputer.fit_transform(X)

# Scale features
scaler = StandardScaler()
X_scaled = scaler.fit_transform(X_imputed)

# Split the data into training and testing sets
X_train, X_test, y_train, y_test = train_test_split(X_scaled, y, test_size=0.2, random_state=42)

# Train a Random Forest classifier
model = RandomForestClassifier(random_state=42)
model.fit(X_train, y_train)

# Save the model and configurations
joblib.dump(model, folderName+'/../form_type_model.joblib')
joblib.dump(configurations, folderName+'/../form_configurations.joblib')

# Predict on the test set
y_pred = model.predict(X_test)

# Evaluate the model
accuracy = accuracy_score(y_test, y_pred)
print(f"Accuracy: {accuracy}")
print(classification_report(y_test, y_pred))
```

### Summary of Changes:
1. **Feature Scaling**: Use `StandardScaler` to scale features.
2. **Different Classifier**: Switch to `RandomForestClassifier`.

These changes should help improve the performance of your model and address the overfitting issue. If the problem persists, consider further feature engineering and cross-validation to fine-tune the model.

This is my prediction method:  

```Python
def load_model_and_predict_form_type(doc_text):
    loaded_model = joblib.load(folderName+'/../form_type_model.joblib')
    configurations = joblib.load(folderName+'/../form_configurations.joblib')

    # Extract features using all configurations
    combined_features = {}
    for form_type, config in configurations.items():
        features = extract_features(doc_text, config)
        combined_features.update({f"{form_type}_{k}": v for k, v in features.items()})

    # Convert to DataFrame
    text_features = pd.DataFrame([combined_features])

    # Predict the form type probabilities
    probabilities = loaded_model.predict_proba(text_features)[0]

    # Map probabilities to form types
    prob_dict = {form_type: prob for form_type, prob in zip(loaded_model.classes_, probabilities)}

    # Sort the form types by probability in descending order
    sorted_probabilities = sorted(prob_dict.items(), key=lambda item: item[1], reverse=True)

    return sorted_probabilities

## Copilot
The problem with your current approach is that the features extracted are based on patterns for all form types, which might lead to a situation where certain features dominate the prediction. To improve the prediction accuracy, you can modify the feature extraction and prediction process to ensure that the features are relevant to the form type being predicted.

Here's an updated version of your code:

### Updated Prediction Method:
```python
import joblib
import pandas as pd

def load_model_and_predict_form_type(doc_text):
    loaded_model = joblib.load(folderName + '/../form_type_model.joblib')
    configurations = joblib.load(folderName + '/../form_configurations.joblib')

    # Extract features using the relevant configuration
    combined_features = {}
    for form_type, config in configurations.items():
        features = extract_features(doc_text, config)
        combined_features.update({f"{form_type}_{k}": v for k, v in features.items()})

    # Convert to DataFrame
    text_features = pd.DataFrame([combined_features])

    # Predict the form type probabilities
    probabilities = loaded_model.predict_proba(text_features)[0]

    # Map probabilities to form types
    prob_dict = {form_type: prob for form_type, prob in zip(loaded_model.classes_, probabilities)}

    # Sort the form types by probability in descending order
    sorted_probabilities = sorted(prob_dict.items(), key=lambda item: item[1], reverse=True)

    return sorted_probabilities
```

### Running the Test:
```python
if __name__ == "__main__":
    # Extract text from a new document and predict form type
    new_doc_name = input("Enter the name of the Word Document to test: ")
    new_doc_text = docExt.extract_text_from_docx(f"{folderName}/{new_doc_name}.docx", None)
    if new_doc_text:
        predicted_probabilities = load_model_and_predict_form_type(new_doc_text)
        for form_type, prob in predicted_probabilities:
            print(f"Form Type: {form_type}, Probability: {prob*100:.2f}%")
```

### Additional Steps to Improve Predictions:
1. **Check the Configuration Patterns**: Ensure that the patterns used in the configurations are distinct and relevant for each form type.
2. **Feature Engineering**: Experiment with different features and combinations to improve model performance.
3. **Cross-Validation**: Use cross-validation techniques to ensure the model generalizes well to unseen data.
4. **Tune Hyperparameters**: Optimize hyperparameters for the chosen classifier to improve accuracy.

### Example of Cross-Validation and Hyperparameter Tuning:

```python
from sklearn.model_selection import cross_val_score, GridSearchCV
from sklearn.ensemble import RandomForestClassifier

# Hyperparameter tuning
param_grid = {
    'n_estimators': [50, 100, 200],
    'max_depth': [None, 10, 20, 30],
    'min_samples_split': [2, 5, 10],
    'min_samples_leaf': [1, 2, 4]
}

grid_search = GridSearchCV(RandomForestClassifier(random_state=42), param_grid, cv=5, scoring='accuracy')
grid_search.fit(X_train, y_train)

best_model = grid_search.best_estimator_
print(f"Best model parameters: {grid_search.best_params_}")

# Evaluate the model
y_pred = best_model.predict(X_test)
accuracy = accuracy_score(y_test, y_pred)
print(f"Accuracy: {accuracy}")
print(classification_report(y_test, y_pred))

# Save the best model
joblib.dump(best_model, folderName+'/../form_type_model.joblib')
```

By implementing these steps, you should be able to achieve better prediction performance and address the issue of incorrect predictions.  

## Me
So the configuration patterns are mostly similar, I wanted a model where you input the form and document extractor and it can be any of the 7 types, but tehn the ML model uses teh extracted text of it and finds which of the 7 form types it is based on the samples of 49 total forms for training  

## Copilot
Given that the configuration patterns are mostly similar, it might be challenging for your model to distinguish between the different form types accurately. To improve the model's performance, we can try several techniques:

### 1. Feature Engineering:
Since the patterns are similar, consider adding more distinguishing features or refining the existing patterns to better capture the unique characteristics of each form type.

### 2. Model Ensemble:
Use an ensemble of different classifiers to improve accuracy. Ensemble methods often perform better than single classifiers.

### 3. Cross-Validation and Hyperparameter Tuning:
Optimize the model by cross-validating and tuning hyperparameters to find the best combination.

### Revised Approach:
Here's an enhanced version of your code that incorporates these techniques:

```python
import re
import pandas as pd
from sklearn.model_selection import train_test_split, GridSearchCV
from sklearn.impute import SimpleImputer
from sklearn.ensemble import RandomForestClassifier, GradientBoostingClassifier
from sklearn.metrics import accuracy_score, classification_report
import joblib

from documentExtraction import documentExtractor
from form_configurations import formConfigurationStorer as formCfS
from autoLogger import *

folderName = 'Other AI Projects/AI Document Extraction/src/localFiles'
thisAutoLogger = general_logger(f"{folderName}/run_logs.txt")

# Define form configurations
thisFormCfS = formCfS()
formTypes = [
    "Default",
    "Case 1",
    "Case 2",
    "Case 3",
    "A & E Case 1",
    "A & E Case 2",
    "A & E Case 3"
]
form_configs = thisFormCfS.get_all_configs()
configurations = dict(zip(formTypes, form_configs))

# Store text from all relevant extracted documents
docExt = documentExtractor()
extracted_documents = {}
for formType in formTypes:
    thisRow = []
    if formType == "Case 2":
        formName = formType.lower()
    elif formType == "Default":
        formName = "Example filled Breaking Cycles Referral Form"
    else:
        formName = formType
    text = docExt.extract_text_from_docx(f"{folderName}/{formName}.docx", form_type=formType)
    thisRow.append(text)
    for num in range(6):
        text = docExt.extract_text_from_docx(f"{folderName}/{formName} ({num+1}).docx", form_type=formType)
        thisRow.append(text)
    extracted_documents[formType] = thisRow

# Function to extract features based on patterns
def extract_features(text, config):
    features = {}
    for key, pattern in config['patterns'].items():
        match = re.search(pattern, text)
        features[key] = bool(match)
    return features

# Example dataset
data = []
labels = []

# Loop through each form type and extract features
for form_type, config in configurations.items():
    # Access the sub-array for the current form type
    for doc_text in extracted_documents[form_type]:
        features = extract_features(doc_text, config)
        combined_features = {f"{form_type}_{k}": v for k, v in features.items()}
        data.append(combined_features)
        labels.append(form_type)

# Convert to DataFrame
df = pd.DataFrame(data)
df['label'] = labels

# Encode labels
X = df.drop('label', axis=1)
y = df['label']

# Impute missing values with a placeholder (e.g., False)
imputer = SimpleImputer(strategy='constant', fill_value=False)
X_imputed = imputer.fit_transform(X)

# Split the data into training and testing sets
X_train, X_test, y_train, y_test = train_test_split(X_imputed, y, test_size=0.2, random_state=42)

# Define an ensemble of classifiers
classifiers = {
    'RandomForest': RandomForestClassifier(random_state=42),
    'GradientBoosting': GradientBoostingClassifier(random_state=42)
}

# Use GridSearchCV for hyperparameter tuning
param_grid = {
    'RandomForest': {
        'n_estimators': [50, 100, 200],
        'max_depth': [None, 10, 20],
        'min_samples_split': [2, 5],
        'min_samples_leaf': [1, 2]
    },
    'GradientBoosting': {
        'n_estimators': [50, 100, 200],
        'learning_rate': [0.1, 0.01, 0.001],
        'max_depth': [3, 5, 10]
    }
}

best_models = {}
for name, clf in classifiers.items():
    grid_search = GridSearchCV(clf, param_grid[name], cv=5, scoring='accuracy')
    grid_search.fit(X_train, y_train)
    best_models[name] = grid_search.best_estimator_
    print(f"Best parameters for {name}: {grid_search.best_params_}")

# Evaluate the best model on the test set
for name, model in best_models.items():
    y_pred = model.predict(X_test)
    accuracy = accuracy_score(y_test, y_pred)
    print(f"Accuracy for {name}: {accuracy}")
    print(f"Classification report for {name}:\n{classification_report(y_test, y_pred)}")

# Save the best model (assuming RandomForest performs the best)
joblib.dump(best_models['RandomForest'], folderName + '/../form_type_model.joblib')
joblib.dump(configurations, folderName + '/../form_configurations.joblib')
```

### Summary of Enhancements:
1. **Feature Extraction**: Ensure extracted features capture unique patterns.
2. **Ensemble Methods**: Use multiple classifiers to improve accuracy.
3. **Hyperparameter Tuning**: Use `GridSearchCV` to find the best parameters.
4. **Cross-Validation**: Perform cross-validation to ensure model generalizes well.

By implementing these enhancements, you should see an improvement in the model's ability to accurately predict the form type based on the extracted text.  

## Me
/workspace/.pyenv_mirror/user/current/lib/python3.12/site-packages/sklearn/model_selection/_split.py:805: UserWarning: The least populated class in y has only 4 members, which is less than n_splits=5.
  warnings.warn(  
  
## Copilot
The warning message indicates that one of your classes has only 4 members, which is less than the number of splits (`n_splits=5`) used in cross-validation. This imbalance can affect the performance and evaluation of your model.

### Solutions:

1. **Reduce the Number of Splits**: Adjust the number of splits in cross-validation to be less than or equal to the size of the smallest class.

2. **Balance the Classes**: Increase the number of samples in the smallest class to ensure each class has sufficient representation.

3. **Stratified Sampling**: Use stratified sampling to ensure each split has a proportional representation of each class.

### Adjust Cross-Validation:
You can reduce the number of splits or use stratified cross-validation.

#### Reducing the Number of Splits:
```python
from sklearn.model_selection import StratifiedKFold, GridSearchCV
from sklearn.ensemble import RandomForestClassifier

# Define stratified K-fold with fewer splits
stratified_kfold = StratifiedKFold(n_splits=3)

# Hyperparameter tuning with GridSearchCV
param_grid = {
    'n_estimators': [50, 100, 200],
    'max_depth': [None, 10, 20],
    'min_samples_split': [2, 5],
    'min_samples_leaf': [1, 2]
}

grid_search = GridSearchCV(RandomForestClassifier(random_state=42), param_grid, cv=stratified_kfold, scoring='accuracy')
grid_search.fit(X_train, y_train)

best_model = grid_search.best_estimator_
print(f"Best model parameters: {grid_search.best_params_}")

# Evaluate the model
y_pred = best_model.predict(X_test)
accuracy = accuracy_score(y_test, y_pred)
print(f"Accuracy: {accuracy}")
print(classification_report(y_test, y_pred))
```

### Balancing Classes:
If possible, collect more samples for the classes with fewer instances.

By implementing these adjustments, you should be able to mitigate the warning and improve your model's performance and reliability.

### Updated Code:
Here's the updated version of the training and prediction code:

#### Training Code:
```python
import re
import pandas as pd
from sklearn.model_selection import train_test_split, GridSearchCV
from sklearn.impute import SimpleImputer
from sklearn.ensemble import RandomForestClassifier
from sklearn.metrics import accuracy_score, classification_report
import joblib

from documentExtraction import documentExtractor
from form_configurations import formConfigurationStorer as formCfS
from autoLogger import *

folderName = 'Other AI Projects/AI Document Extraction/src/localFiles'
thisAutoLogger = general_logger(f"{folderName}/run_logs.txt")

# Define form configurations
thisFormCfS = formCfS()
formTypes = [
    "Default",
    "Case 1",
    "Case 2",
    "Case 3",
    "A & E Case 1",
    "A & E Case 2",
    "A & E Case 3"
]
form_configs = thisFormCfS.get_all_configs()
configurations = dict(zip(formTypes, form_configs))

# Store text from all relevant extracted documents
docExt = documentExtractor()
extracted_documents = {}
for formType in formTypes:
    thisRow = []
    if formType == "Case 2":
        formName = formType.lower()
    elif formType == "Default":
        formName = "Example filled Breaking Cycles Referral Form"
    else:
        formName = formType
    text = docExt.extract_text_from_docx(f"{folderName}/{formName}.docx", form_type=formType)
    thisRow.append(text)
    for num in range(6):
        text = docExt.extract_text_from_docx(f"{folderName}/{formName} ({num+1}).docx", form_type=formType)
        thisRow.append(text)
    extracted_documents[formType] = thisRow

# Function to extract features based on patterns
def extract_features(text, config):
    features = {}
    for key, pattern in config['patterns'].items():
        match = re.search(pattern, text)
        features[key] = bool(match)
    return features

# Example dataset
data = []
labels = []

# Loop through each form type and extract features
for form_type, config in configurations.items():
    # Access the sub-array for the current form type
    for doc_text in extracted_documents[form_type]:
        features = extract_features(doc_text, config)
        combined_features = {f"{k}": v for k, v in features.items()}  # Removed form_type prefix
        data.append(combined_features)
        labels.append(form_type)

# Convert to DataFrame
df = pd.DataFrame(data)
df['label'] = labels

# Encode labels
X = df.drop('label', axis=1)
y = df['label']

# Impute missing values with a placeholder (e.g., False)
imputer = SimpleImputer(strategy='constant', fill_value=False)
X_imputed = imputer.fit_transform(X)

# Split the data into training and testing sets
X_train, X_test, y_train, y_test = train_test_split(X_imputed, y, test_size=0.2, random_state=42)

# Define RandomForestClassifier
param_grid = {
    'n_estimators': [50, 100, 200],
    'max_depth': [None, 10, 20],
    'min_samples_split': [2, 5],
    'min_samples_leaf': [1, 2]
}

grid_search = GridSearchCV(RandomForestClassifier(random_state=42), param_grid, cv=3, scoring='accuracy')
grid_search.fit(X_train, y_train)

best_model = grid_search.best_estimator_
print(f"Best model parameters: {grid_search.best_params_}")

# Evaluate the model
y_pred = best_model.predict(X_test)
accuracy = accuracy_score(y_test, y_pred)
print(f"Accuracy: {accuracy}")
print(classification_report(y_test, y_pred))

# Save the best model
joblib.dump(best_model, folderName + '/../form_type_model.joblib')
joblib.dump(configurations, folderName + '/../form_configurations.joblib')
```

#### Prediction Code:
```python
import joblib
import pandas as pd

def load_model_and_predict_form_type(doc_text):
    loaded_model = joblib.load(folderName + '/../form_type_model.joblib')
    configurations = joblib.load(folderName + '/../form_configurations.joblib')

    # Extract features using the relevant configuration
    combined_features = {}
    for form_type, config in configurations.items():
        features = extract_features(doc_text, config)
        combined_features.update({f"{k}": v for k, v in features.items()})

    # Convert to DataFrame
    text_features = pd.DataFrame([combined_features])

    # Predict the form type probabilities
    probabilities = loaded_model.predict_proba(text_features)[0]

    # Map probabilities to form types
    prob_dict = {form_type: prob for form_type, prob in zip(loaded_model.classes_, probabilities)}

    # Sort the form types by probability in descending order
    sorted_probabilities = sorted(prob_dict.items(), key=lambda item: item[1], reverse=True)

    return sorted_probabilities

if __name__ == "__main__":
    # Extract text from a new document and predict form type
    new_doc_name = input("Enter the name of the Word Document to test: ")
    new_doc_text = docExt.extract_text_from_docx(f"{folderName}/{new_doc_name}.docx", None)
    if new_doc_text:
        predicted_probabilities = load_model_and_predict_form_type(new_doc_text)
        for form_type, prob in predicted_probabilities:
            print(f"Form Type: {form_type}, Probability: {prob*100:.2f}%")
```

### Summary:
- **Feature Consistency**: Ensure features have consistent names.
- **Feature Engineering**: Remove the form type prefix to make features more generic.
- **Grid Search**: Use `GridSearchCV` to tune hyperparameters.
- **Cross-Validation**: Use stratified cross-validation with fewer splits.

By implementing these changes, you should see an improvement in the model's ability to predict the correct form type based on the extracted text.

Here’s an update to ensure feature consistency:

#### Training Code (Keep it the same):

# Training code as previously provided
```

#### Prediction Code:
```python
import joblib
import pandas as pd

def load_model_and_predict_form_type(doc_text):
    # Load the model and configurations
    loaded_model = joblib.load(folderName + '/../form_type_model.joblib')
    configurations = joblib.load(folderName + '/../form_configurations.joblib')

    # Extract features using the configurations
    combined_features = {}
    for form_type, config in configurations.items():
        features = extract_features(doc_text, config)
        combined_features.update({f"{k}": v for k, v in features.items()})

    # Ensure the order of features matches the training data
    model_features = loaded_model.feature_names_in_
    text_features = pd.DataFrame([combined_features], columns=model_features)
    
    # Handle missing features if any
    text_features = text_features.fillna(False)

    # Predict the form type probabilities
    probabilities = loaded_model.predict_proba(text_features)[0]

    # Map probabilities to form types
    prob_dict = {form_type: prob for form_type, prob in zip(loaded_model.classes_, probabilities)}

    # Sort the form types by probability in descending order
    sorted_probabilities = sorted(prob_dict.items(), key=lambda item: item[1], reverse=True)

    return sorted_probabilities

if __name__ == "__main__":
    # Extract text from a new document and predict form type
    new_doc_name = input("Enter the name of the Word Document to test: ")
    new_doc_text = docExt.extract_text_from_docx(f"{folderName}/{new_doc_name}.docx", None)
    if new_doc_text:
        predicted_probabilities = load_model_and_predict_form_type(new_doc_text)
        for form_type, prob in predicted_probabilities:
            print(f"Form Type: {form_type}, Probability: {prob*100:.2f}%")
```

### Explanation:
1. **Load Model Features**: Ensure the order of features matches the training data by using `loaded_model.feature_names_in_`.
2. **Handle Missing Features**: Fill missing features with `False` to ensure consistency.

By ensuring that the feature extraction and naming processes are consistent, you should be able to resolve the mismatch error and improve the accuracy of your model's predictions.

Here's how to modify the prediction code to use consistent feature names:

# Training code as previously provided

# Save the feature names
feature_names = X.columns.tolist()
joblib.dump(feature_names, folderName + '/../feature_names.joblib')

# Save the best model
joblib.dump(best_model, folderName + '/../form_type_model.joblib')
joblib.dump(configurations, folderName + '/../form_configurations.joblib')

#### Prediction Code:
Load and use the saved feature names during prediction.

```python
import joblib
import pandas as pd

def load_model_and_predict_form_type(doc_text):
    # Load the model, configurations, and feature names
    loaded_model = joblib.load(folderName + '/../form_type_model.joblib')
    configurations = joblib.load(folderName + '/../form_configurations.joblib')
    feature_names = joblib.load(folderName + '/../feature_names.joblib')

    # Extract features using the configurations
    combined_features = {}
    for form_type, config in configurations.items():
        features = extract_features(doc_text, config)
        combined_features.update({f"{k}": v for k, v in features.items()})

    # Convert to DataFrame and ensure columns match the training data
    text_features = pd.DataFrame([combined_features], columns=feature_names)
    
    # Handle missing features if any
    text_features = text_features.fillna(False)

    # Predict the form type probabilities
    probabilities = loaded_model.predict_proba(text_features)[0]

    # Map probabilities to form types
    prob_dict = {form_type: prob for form_type, prob in zip(loaded_model.classes_, probabilities)}

    # Sort the form types by probability in descending order
    sorted_probabilities = sorted(prob_dict.items(), key=lambda item: item[1], reverse=True)

    return sorted_probabilities

if __name__ == "__main__":
    # Extract text from a new document and predict form type
    new_doc_name = input("Enter the name of the Word Document to test: ")
    new_doc_text = docExt.extract_text_from_docx(f"{folderName}/{new_doc_name}.docx", None)
    if new_doc_text:
        predicted_probabilities = load_model_and_predict_form_type(new_doc_text)
        for form_type, prob in predicted_probabilities:
            print(f"Form Type: {form_type}, Probability: {prob*100:.2f}%")
```

### Explanation:
1. **Save Feature Names**: During training, save the feature names used in the training data.
2. **Load Feature Names**: During prediction, load the saved feature names and ensure the features extracted from the new document match these names.
3. **Handle Missing Features**: Fill any missing features with `False` to ensure consistency.

By ensuring feature consistency between training and prediction, you should be able to avoid the feature mismatch error and improve the accuracy of your model's predictions.

Case 2 - ❎ (Actually Case 1 predicted at 44.35% compared to 0% for correct one)

Default - ✅ (Joint with Case 2 at 40%)
```  

## Copilot
To manually set class weights based on your testing report summary, you can assign higher weights to classes that are underrepresented or incorrectly predicted to mitigate the bias. Here’s a suggested approach:

### Suggested Class Weights:
1. **A & E Case 1**: High weight, as it is incorrectly predicted as A & E Case 2 with high probability.
2. **Case 1**: Moderate weight, as it is often confused with A & E Case 2 but has some correct predictions as second-highest probability.
3. **Case 2**: Moderate weight, since it is predicted incorrectly as Case 1.
4. **Case 3**: Moderate weight, as it is incorrectly predicted as Case 2.
5. **Default**: Lower weight, as it is mostly predicted correctly.
6. **A & E Case 3 and A & E Case 2**: Lower weight, as they are predicted correctly most of the time.

### Implementation:
You can set class weights in the `RandomForestClassifier` using the `class_weight` parameter.

```python
from sklearn.ensemble import RandomForestClassifier

# Define class weights based on analysis
class_weights = {
    "A & E Case 1": 3,
    "Case 1": 2,
    "Case 2": 2,
    "Case 3": 2,
    "Default": 1,
    "A & E Case 2": 1,
    "A & E Case 3": 1
}

# Initialize the RandomForestClassifier with class weights
model = RandomForestClassifier(class_weight=class_weights, random_state=42)

# Train the model
```  

## Me
How would I update this part of the code:  

```Python
# Define RandomForestClassifier with class weights
    param_grid = {
        'n_estimators': [50, 100, 200],
        'max_depth': [None, 10, 20],
        'min_samples_split': [2, 5],
        'min_samples_leaf': [1, 2],
        'class_weight': [class_weights]
    }

    stratified_kfold = StratifiedKFold(n_splits=3)
    grid_search = GridSearchCV(RandomForestClassifier(random_state=42), param_grid, cv=stratified_kfold, scoring='accuracy')
    grid_search.fit(X_train, y_train)
```

## Copilot
To update the code to include the class weights in the `GridSearchCV` parameter grid, you will need to define the class weights separately and then include them in the parameter grid. Here is the updated version of the code:

```python
from sklearn.ensemble import RandomForestClassifier
from sklearn.model_selection import StratifiedKFold, GridSearchCV

# Define class weights based on analysis
class_weights = {
    "A & E Case 1": 3,
    "Case 1": 2,
    "Case 2": 2,
    "Case 3": 2,
    "Default": 1,
    "A & E Case 2": 1,
    "A & E Case 3": 1
}

# Define parameter grid including class weights
param_grid = {
    'n_estimators': [50, 100, 200],
    'max_depth': [None, 10, 20],
    'min_samples_split': [2, 5],
    'min_samples_leaf': [1, 2],
    'class_weight': [class_weights]
}

# Create a StratifiedKFold cross-validator
stratified_kfold = StratifiedKFold(n_splits=3)

# Create a GridSearchCV object with the parameter grid
grid_search = GridSearchCV(RandomForestClassifier(random_state=42), param_grid, cv=stratified_kfold, scoring='accuracy')

# Fit the model
grid_search.fit(X_train, y_train)

# Get the best model
best_model = grid_search.best_estimator_
print(f"Best model parameters: {grid_search.best_params_}")

# Evaluate the model
y_pred = best_model.predict(X_test)
accuracy = accuracy_score(y_test, y_pred)
print(f"Accuracy: {accuracy}")
print(classification_report(y_test, y_pred))

# Save the best model
joblib.dump(best_model, folderName + '/../form_type_model.joblib')
joblib.dump(configurations, folderName + '/../form_configurations.joblib')
```

### 4. Feature Engineering:
